## Section 001: Skill Installer Distribution Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Skill Installer Distribution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed no seed line states what this theme actually is, a 58-line preinstalled Codex system skill that turns GitHub directories into an installable skill registry, distributing skills from a three-tier upstream, curated, experimental, and preinstalled system tiers under openai/skills, plus arbitrary public or private repos, through two helper scripts and a defaults-plus-fallback download strategy
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Skill Installer Distribution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Codex needed skill distribution without a package manager, so the installer skill maps registry semantics onto plain GitHub structure, directories as packages, refs as versions, the API for listing and download-or-git for fetching, a distribution system built entirely from repository conventions
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Skill Installer Distribution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: reading this as authoring guidance misses its category, the installer never teaches how to write skills, it defines how finished skills move from repos into $CODEX_HOME/skills and what the agent must say and do at each step
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Skill Installer Distribution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference covers skill distribution mechanics, skill authoring and evaluation belong to the creator-lineage themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Skill Installer Distribution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the registry-from-GitHub framing, the three-tier upstream, and the 58-line single-source evidence base
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Skill Installer Distribution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the installer is itself distributed by the mechanism it implements, it lives in the .system tier its own notes describe as preinstalled, a distribution tool shipped through its own channel, which is why its notes must special-case users asking to install it or its siblings, the bootstrap tier cannot be installed normally because it is already there

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Skill Installer Distribution Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference covers skill distribution mechanics, skill authoring and evaluation belong to the creator-lineage themes

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed one local row is the entire evidence base, a 58-line document with no sibling in any other sweep and no live-tree twin, making this the corpus's leanest theme, no identity diffs were possible and none of the multi-source triangulation richer themes enjoy applies here
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the installer appears only in the 202603 Codex sweep, so every claim in this reference chains back to a single dated snapshot of a single file, evidence concentration by necessity rather than choice
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the risk of a one-source theme is invisible staleness, nothing in the repository can contradict or corroborate the snapshot, so overconfident reuse treats one month's text as standing truth
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: provenance for this document's statements, the three external URLs stayed unretrieved and confer no current-fact authority
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to annotate the mapping with the single-source condition, the absent-twin fact, and the resulting all-claims-archive-dated rule
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that single-source themes invert the duplication problem the skill-creator themes solved, there the work was discounting redundant copies, here the work is refusing to inflate one copy, the honest evidence statement is one file, one month, one platform, and every synthesis sentence must be built to survive on that

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand beside the source's own retry doctrine, the method ladder is a designed retry sequence, download, then git over HTTPS, then SSH, each rung triggered by the previous rung's specific failure class, with two hard stops, the existing-destination abort that no retry may bypass, and the unavailable-listing rule, explain the error and exit rather than hammer the API
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because distribution retries are fallback-shaped rather than repeat-shaped, retrying the same failed method reproduces the same auth wall, so the ladder changes strategy per attempt instead of repeating one
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: repeat-shaped retries against the GitHub API risk rate limiting and mask the real failure class, while retrying past the abort would convert a safety stop into an overwrite
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: retry semantics in skill distribution, evaluation-iteration retry rules belong to the sibling theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the ladder as strategy-changing retries with failure-class triggers and the two hard stops as retry boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the source distinguishes recoverable from unrecoverable failures structurally, transport failures get the ladder, state conflicts and upstream absence get honest termination, encoding in 58 lines the classification that retry doctrine usually spells out in pages, what can change on the next attempt determines whether a next attempt exists

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed latency packet stands beside the source's actual performance choices, direct download as the default because it is the fast path, git sparse checkout as the fallback because it trades speed for auth compatibility, sparse rather than full checkout to fetch only the skill's subtree, and batch multi-path installs to amortize one invocation across several skills
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because distribution performance is dominated by transfer scope and round trips, so the source's choices all shrink one or the other, download skips git overhead, sparseness skips the repo bulk, batching skips repeated startup
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: inverting the defaults, git-first fetching or full clones for one skill directory, multiplies transfer cost for no resilience gain, the ladder already provides the fallback when the fast path fails
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: performance of the distribution operation, installed skills' context costs belong to the platform and creator themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the three performance choices with their rationales and the ladder as the mechanism that keeps the fast default safe
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that sparse checkout is the design's quiet efficiency commitment, even the fallback path refuses to fetch more than the skill's subtree, so the performance principle holds at every rung, transfer scope tracks the artifact, not the repository, a rule worth exporting to any repo-subset distribution tool
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to keep download-first, sparse fallbacks, and batch invocations, measuring only when installs feel slow
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because distribution performance is dominated by transfer scope and round trips, so the source's choices all shrink one or the other, download skips git overhead, sparseness skips the repo bulk, batching skips repeated startup
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; inverting the defaults, git-first fetching or full clones for one skill directory, multiplies transfer cost for no resilience gain, the ladder already provides the fallback when the fast path fails
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: performance of the distribution operation, installed skills' context costs belong to the platform and creator themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: state the three performance choices with their rationales and the ladder as the mechanism that keeps the fast default safe
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies sparse checkout is the design's quiet efficiency commitment, even the fallback path refuses to fetch more than the skill's subtree, so the performance principle holds at every rung, transfer scope tracks the artifact, not the repository, a rule worth exporting to any repo-subset distribution tool

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed task-splitting bounds stand beside the design's own scale assumptions, the installer serves one user installing single-digit skills per session into one $CODEX_HOME, its consent dialogue, per-request escalation, and abort-and-ask conflict handling all assume a human in the loop, and its upstream assumption is a repository small enough to list conversationally as a numbered catalog
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every mechanism scales with conversation, listing is a numbered chat message, conflicts become questions, and installs need per-run consent, so throughput is bounded by dialogue, not bandwidth
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: past the conversational scale, fleet provisioning, hundreds of skills, unattended automation, the dialogue becomes the bottleneck and the safety semantics, ask-on-conflict, insist-to-override, have no non-interactive answer
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: bounding the installer's designed operating range, larger distribution architectures are beyond the source
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to name the three scale assumptions, single user, catalog-sized upstream, conversational consent, and mark everything beyond them as design territory the source does not cover
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the numbered-list format is the upstream size bound made visible, a catalog that cannot be presented as a short numbered message with a which-ones question has outgrown the interaction model, the communication template is quietly also the scalability specification
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to use the installer within its conversational envelope and treat bulk or unattended needs as new design problems, not flag combinations
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because every mechanism scales with conversation, listing is a numbered chat message, conflicts become questions, and installs need per-run consent, so throughput is bounded by dialogue, not bandwidth

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: bounding the installer's designed operating range, larger distribution architectures are beyond the source
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: name the three scale assumptions, single user, catalog-sized upstream, conversational consent, and mark everything beyond them as design territory the source does not cover
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the numbered-list format is the upstream size bound made visible, a catalog that cannot be presented as a short numbered message with a which-ones question has outgrown the interaction model, the communication template is quietly also the scalability specification

- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because every mechanism scales with conversation, listing is a numbered chat message, conflicts become questions, and installs need per-run consent, so throughput is bounded by dialogue, not bandwidth

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: past the conversational scale, fleet provisioning, hundreds of skills, unattended automation, the dialogue becomes the bottleneck and the safety semantics, ask-on-conflict, insist-to-override, have no non-interactive answer
